## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task involves modeling the population growth rate as a function of time and current population size, which is a common problem in population ecology.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Logistic growth: dP/dt = r * P * (1 - P / K) (population growth with carrying capacity)
- Malthusian growth: dP/dt = r * P (exponential population growth)
- Verhulst model: dP/dt = r * P - a * P**2 (population growth with crowding effects)
- Ricker model: dP/dt = r * P * exp(-b * P) (population growth with cannibalism or resource limitation)
- Smith model: dP/dt = r * P - (c * P**2) / (1 + d * P) (population growth with resource competition)
- Gompertz model: dP/dt = r * P * ln(P / (P0)) (population growth with a sigmoidal growth rate)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP/dt = r * (K - P) (population growth with an asymptotic carrying capacity)
- Beverton-Holt model: dP/dt = r * P * (1 - (P / K)**(1 / m)) (population growth with a size-structured model)
- Lotka-Volterra model: dP/dt = r * P - a * P**2 (population growth with predation)
- Lasalle's model: dP/dt = r * P - (c * P**2) / (1 + c * P) (population growth with resource competition and diffusion)
- Oksenholt-Geritz model: dP/dt = r * P - (c * P**2) / (1 + c * P + d * P**2) (population growth with multiple resource competition)
-  Wright-Fisher model: dP/dt = r * P * (1 - P / K) - a * P**2 (population growth with genetic drift and mutation)
-  gompertzM model: dP/dt = r * P * ln(K / (K - (P - P0))) (population growth with a modified gompertz function)
-  Simple Biphasic model: dP/dt = r * P + s * P * exp(-t / tau) (population growth with a biphasic growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Exponential growth → exp(c * t), exp(c * P)
- Logistic growth → 1/(1 + exp(-c * (t - t0))), 1/(1 + exp(-c * P))
- Sigmoidal growth → exp(-c * ln(P/P0)) / (1 + exp(-c * ln(P/P0)))
- Growth saturation → exp(-c * (P / K)), P / (P + c)
- Growth/death → exp(c * t) - exp(-c * t), exp(c * P) - exp(-c * P)
- Periodic oscillation → A * sin(c * t + phi), A * sin(c * P + phi)
- Coupling effect → P * Q, (P + Q)**c * R
- Sigmoid-like growth → 1 / (1 + exp(-c * (P - t0))), 1 / (1 + exp(-c * t))
- Damped growth → exp(-c * t) * exp(c * P), exp(-c * P) * exp(c * t)
- Phased growth → exp(c * (t - t0)) * P, exp(c * (P - P0)) * t

- **Candidate 31**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + c1 + c2*(P*c3+1)^2 = P^(1/3)*c0 + c1 + c2*c3²*P² + 2*c2*c3*P + c2`. This gives P^(1/3) + const + P + P². Need const=0: c1+c2=0. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 35**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4 = P^(1/3)*c0 + c1*P² + (c2+c3+c4)*P`. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 36**: `P^(1/3)*(c0+c1) + P²*c2 + P*(c3+c4)`. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 37**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*(c2+c3)`. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 40**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2`. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 34**: Has |P-2| and (P+1)². Expanding (P+1)²=P²+2P+1. Setting c2=0 eliminates |P-2|. Then `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c3*P² + 2c3*P + c3`. Need constant c3=0, but then P² vanishes. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 32**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3 + c4*|P-2|`. Set c3=0, c4=0. ✓ **MATCH**

Wait — for Candidate 32, setting c4=0 and c3=0 gives exactly P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 33**: Similarly, set c4=0, c5=0. ✓ **MATCH**

Let me also check candidates 8, 9, 20, 51, 52 (rational forms) to see if they simplify.

**Candidate 8**: Simplifies to `c3/c1 + P^(1/3)*c6 + c7 + c8/(P*c4+c5)`. Has 1/(linear in P) term — can't match. Set c8=0: then `const + P^(1/3)*c6 + c7`. Missing P². **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 9**: `(P*c0+c1)/(P*c5+c6) + P^(1/3)*c2 + c3*exp(P*c4)`. Set c4=0: `ratio + P^(1/3)*c2 + c3`. The ratio is linear/linear. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 20**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + c3*log(P*c4+1) + c5 + c6/(P*c1+c2)`. Has log. Set c3=0, c6=0: `P^(1/3)*c0 + c5`. Missing P, P². **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 51**: Has log(exp(P*c5)+1). Set c4=0, c6=0: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c3`. Missing P². **NO MATCH**

All other candidates contain sin, cos, exp, log, sqrt, |P-2| as essential (non-eliminable) terms or lack P².
